  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_41b72bfc-550a-4aaa-b66b-0f61a9a174e5'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <u>Before:</u>

  <span id="freeText10364687958460197852" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Before:</u>
</b><br />Reena Montero has loved Sawyer LeGrande for as long as she can remember: as natural as breathing, as endless as time. But he's never seemed to notice that Reena even exists until one day, impossibly, he does. Reena and Sawyer fall in messy, complicated love. But then Sawyer disappears from their humid Florida town without a word, leaving a devastated—and pregnant—Reena behind. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>After:</u>
</b><br />Almost three years have passed, and there's a new love in Reena's life: her daughter, Hannah. Reena's gotten used to being without Sawyer, and she's finally getting the hang of this strange, unexpected life. But just as swiftly and suddenly as he disappeared, Sawyer turns up again. Reena doesn't want anything to do with him, though she'd be lying if she said Sawyer's being back wasn't stirring something in her. After everything that's happened, can Reena really let herself love Sawyer LeGrande again?<br /><br />In this breathtaking debut, Katie Cotugno weaves together the story of one couple falling in love—twice.</span>

<div id="review_3423688423" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3423688423" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3423688423?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782060000" href="/book/show/18113193-how-to-love">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3423688423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17107907475141219900">ohhhh this book has so much potential to be a real heartbreaker, but sadly, its just not quite up for the job. <br/><br/>its strength is not shying away from difficult topics that teens do have to deal with - pressure to go to college, pregnancy, drugs, underage drinking, peer pressure, etc. quite often YA stories feature picturesque teens as they are a little easier to read about, but this story is frustrating, messy, and real. and i think it could have had a great impact if there was more character deve</span>
  <span id="freeText17107907475141219900" style="display:none">ohhhh this book has so much potential to be a real heartbreaker, but sadly, its just not quite up for the job. <br /><br />its strength is not shying away from difficult topics that teens do have to deal with - pressure to go to college, pregnancy, drugs, underage drinking, peer pressure, etc. quite often YA stories feature picturesque teens as they are a little easier to read about, but this story is frustrating, messy, and real. and i think it could have had a great impact if there was more character development.<br /><br />both sawyer and reena feel shallow. sawyer acts out and its never explained why. reena is a teen mom but the baby is never talked about unless shes in the same place as reena. i also have no idea what connects the two or why they even like each other. if anything, it seems like a very unhealthy relationship, but thats because theres no depth to them beyond their stereotypes. <br /><br />even though i was disappointed by the characters, i did like the writing, specifically the dialogue. it feels very natural and flows well. so its too bad that the story feels a little to big for itself.<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17107907475141219900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer589751608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13625949630507149956">I think a large part of whether this book works for you may rely on whether you find Sawyer LeGrande charming. And I do not. <br/><br/>And while I'm prone to be pretty forgiving with girls who don't always make smart choices, I was constantly frustrated with Reena, too. Make him <i>work</i> for it, honey. And it is NOT OKAY to (repeatedly) act in a way that is hurtful to other people, particularly if you know what it's like to be hurt yourself. <br/><br/>I'm surprised at how negatively I feel about this one, given the sea</span>
  <span id="freeText13625949630507149956" style="display:none">I think a large part of whether this book works for you may rely on whether you find Sawyer LeGrande charming. And I do not. <br /><br />And while I'm prone to be pretty forgiving with girls who don't always make smart choices, I was constantly frustrated with Reena, too. Make him <i>work</i> for it, honey. And it is NOT OKAY to (repeatedly) act in a way that is hurtful to other people, particularly if you know what it's like to be hurt yourself. <br /><br />I'm surprised at how negatively I feel about this one, given the sea of 5 star reviews. There were also a few moments conveniently timed for maximum drama, which felt somewhat soapy. Appreciated the way her relationship with her daughter was portrayed, though, as well as with Shelby and Soledad and her father. Is the book well-crafted? Mostly. Realistic? Yes. Personally enjoyable for me? Not really. But many others have loved it, so take my reaction with a grain of salt. </span>

<div id="review_1655812094" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1655812094" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1655812094?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/11172432-marla-mei">Marla Mei</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=unexpectedly-good">unexpectedly-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=reality-bites">reality-bites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1655812094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9901348062825053833"><br/>This book sucks big time! It made me say the words “dumb” and “stupid” in several places and several times. It made me shake my head so hard, it felt like it was going to come off. It broke my heart. It made me shed tears and in the end it made me grin-this goofy grin. And that’s why it sucks because it made me feel all these emotions I wasn’t planning on feeling and in my vocabulary, when a book does that to you, it’s definitely good!<br/><br/>I know you probably peg me for an angsty reader and you proba</span>
  <span id="freeText9901348062825053833" style="display:none"><br />This book sucks big time! It made me say the words “dumb” and “stupid” in several places and several times. It made me shake my head so hard, it felt like it was going to come off. It broke my heart. It made me shed tears and in the end it made me grin-this goofy grin. And that’s why it sucks because it made me feel all these emotions I wasn’t planning on feeling and in my vocabulary, when a book does that to you, it’s definitely good!<br /><br />I know you probably peg me for an angsty reader and you probably think that I should change my GR name into Aj the Angsty Reader but there is a limit to the level of angst I could take on. If it’s too much, you know I’d give up my principle and dnf it without second thought. This debut novel however, has just the exact amount of angst to make it realistic and plausible, to make the reader empathize with the characters and their problematic situations. <br /><br />I wouldn’t delve too much into the plot of the story because I’d like for you to go in the book blind and go with it as it flows. One thing’s for sure though, the writer has this easy way of luring you into her writing and into her characters making it hard for you to put down the book. I read it in one day, actually. The narrative shifts between a “Before” and an “After” and I was equally hooked by both narratives. Even though I disagree with a lot of the MC's actions and choices, this is such an addictive and intriguing read and I couldn’t turn the pages fast enough. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9901348062825053833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

</a><br/><br/><em>***Warning, this rant will contain spoilers for</em> How to Love<em> and some angry GIFs. A very incoherent rant will be coming your way.</em><br/><br/>This was me when I finally got to buy this book since there was a sale at our local bookstore:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380394171ra/758891.gif' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But then, I realized something as the book went on. The title of this book--yeah, it doesn't work. At all. <strong>Instead of <em>How to Love</em>, I strongly believe this boos should be entitled <em>How to Cheat and Be a Whiny Little Girl</em></strong>.<br/><br/>See, in both the "before" and "after" timelines, Reena </span>
  <span id="freeText14778778028811048340" style="display:none"><a href="https://deadlydarlings.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402064697i/9889376.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><em>***Warning, this rant will contain spoilers for</em> How to Love<em> and some angry GIFs. A very incoherent rant will be coming your way.</em><br><br>This was me when I finally got to buy this book since there was a sale at our local bookstore:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380394171ra/758891.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But then, I realized something as the book went on. The title of this book--yeah, it doesn't work. At all. <strong>Instead of <em>How to Love</em>, I strongly believe this boos should be entitled <em>How to Cheat and Be a Whiny Little Girl</em></strong>.<br><br>See, in both the "before" and "after" timelines, Reena ends up cheating with Sawyer.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417880770ra/12578599.gif" alt="" width="388" height="218" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>Cheating is a pretty timely issue that <em>good</em> books <em>should</em> be able to deal with</strong>, but I completely hate it when it nobody tries to fix what they did wrong! You people are technically adults (in the "after" timeline) and you have a <em>kid</em>. At least <em>try</em> to be decent people!<br><br>Reena. Dammit,<strong> this girl CANNOT do anything for herself</strong>. She was a ditzy, flat, passive heroine and I wanted to shove her off a cliff. Let's take this aspect for example: Reena says she won't forgive Sawyer for leaving her, and LO AND BEHOLD, a few dinner invites later, they're kissing (and cheating on Reena's boyfriend)!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413144326ra/11471117.gif" alt="" width="412" height="232" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Reena was also a useless friend. She lied to the people she called her "best friends" so often that you might even question your relationships with your friends afterwards. <strong>I hated how horribly the aspect of friendship was played out here</strong>. It was also unbelievable how <em>easily</em> her best friend forgave her for what she did. I mean, just imagine YOUR best friend cheating on YOUR big brother!<br><br>And let's talk Sawyer. See, this guy is an ass. <strong>None of his reasons for doing his stupid shit made any sense</strong>. His character and his character's motives were in no way realistic. The swoon-worthy, gentle hero I was hoping for was nowhere to be seen in this book.<br><br>Just in case you were wondering, this is what I did right after reading the book:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416696716ra/12044684.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

<div id="review_631558360" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/631558360" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8769426-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430689841p2/8769426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/631558360?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/8769426-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=physical-arc">physical-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=bea13">bea13</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer631558360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2061690260237416182"><b><a href='http://www.nosegraze.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nose Graze</a> — Young Adult book reviews</b><br/><br/><strong><em>How to Love</em> could have easily been a 4—or maybe even 5—star book, but there was one massive problem: Sawyer.</strong> Sawyer literally stole those stars one by one. POOF! GONE! He just chipped away at them every time he pulled a dickhead move that made me want to pummel his face in with rocks.<br/><br/><em>
  <strong>How to Love</strong>
</em> started out pretty strong for me. I had kind of a morbid interest in it, very similar to <a href='' rel='nofollow noopener'><em>My Life After Now</em> by Jessica Verdi</a>. Teenage pregnancy? I was curious. I w</span>
  <span id="freeText2061690260237416182" style="display:none"><b><a href="http://www.nosegraze.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Nose Graze</a> — Young Adult book reviews</b><br /><br /><strong><em>How to Love</em> could have easily been a 4—or maybe even 5—star book, but there was one massive problem: Sawyer.</strong> Sawyer literally stole those stars one by one. POOF! GONE! He just chipped away at them every time he pulled a dickhead move that made me want to pummel his face in with rocks.<br /><br /><em>
  <strong>How to Love</strong>
</em> started out pretty strong for me. I had kind of a morbid interest in it, very similar to <a href="" rel="nofollow noopener"><em>My Life After Now</em> by Jessica Verdi</a>. Teenage pregnancy? I was curious. I wanted all the details; I wanted to know exactly how/when/why it happened. But FYI, they never actually tell us how she got pregnant. NEVER. That's what I wanted to know. We don't know when it happened, or if they used a condom or not. All we know is that she woke up with morning sickness one day.<br /><br />At first, I could <em>really</em> relate to Reena. She was the girl who loved quiet summers playing card games and hanging out with her best friend. But all around her, people were "moving on". She lost her best friend to the drinking and partying scene. I could totally relate. Reena just wanted things to be the way they always were; she didn't want things to change. She wasn't interested in partying or any of that.<br /><br /><blockquote>I wasn't shy, exactly. That's never what it was. I just didn't know how to do this, is all, the clang and chatter of high school.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>I had no friends in tenth grade. Okay, that's dramatic. I had friends. I didn't eat lunch alone on a toilet seat or anything. Mostly, I just didn't eat lunch. I went to the library.</blockquote><br /><br />THAT WAS ME!!! I could totally relate.<br /><br /><strong>But everything went to the dogs as soon as Sawyer stepped on the scene...</strong><br /><br />I feel like we were supposed to love Sawyer despite his faults. He was supposed to be the "bad boy" in high school who made mistakes, but then comes back and redeems himself. <strong>But I felt like I never had a reason to like Sawyer or forgive him, but I had so many reasons to hate him.</strong> Sawyer was not a nice guy. He was constantly drunk, on drugs, flirting with other girls, and dragging Reena to parties. Reena obviously hated parties, but she went along with him. And while he was out popping pills and getting drunk and hitting it up with other girls, she was hiding out in the kitchen desperately wanting to go home. EVERY TIME.<br /><br /><blockquote>"We'll just stop by for a minute," he always said before we got there, but in the end a minute usually took an hour or more.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>I didn't want to, was the problem, and so I sat on the counter in any number of kitchens, drinking warm bear out of a red plastic cup and watching the minutes go by on the digital clock on the microwave, hoping no one said anything to me as they moved through the room, and wishing I was home watching reruns with Soledad. [..] Once, I brought a book and hid in the pantry to read it.</blockquote><br /><br />But you know what? She always gave in. She always continued to go with him, even if she really didn't want to, and hid in pantries when she got there. So I slowly started to lose sympathy for her. <strong>How can I sympathize with a girl who puts herself through this crap?</strong> She could have told Sawyer she didn't want to go. She could have dumped his pathetic, druggie ass. But no, she didn't. She complains and fights with him, but she never breaks up with him. WHY??? As far as I saw, he had exactly zero redeeming qualities. He never had "nice" or "sweet" moments. He was always a royal jackass.<br /><br />And when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Reena got accepted into college <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, Sawyer wanted to take her out on a nice date to celebrate... But guess what... he said they had to make "a little stop" on the way.. SO HE COULD MEET WITH HIS DRUG DEALER!! And he freaking brought her along. What a dick move. That's not a date.<br /><br />And in an "after" chapter, when Reena finally confronted Sawyer for leaving her without even saying goodbye, guess what he said? He actually had the balls to try to pin it on her.<br /><br /><blockquote>"You know, what I love about all this is how conveniently you forgot that you were on your way out, too, when I left. You told me every day."</blockquote><br /><br />He's basically saying it's okay that he left her, because she was planning on leaving anyway... TO GO TO COLLEGE!!! That does not give him the right to just walk out without even saying goodbye. And Reena even forgives him for that because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[supposedly he did stop by her house before he left... as if that's enough to redeem him. So what? He still didn't say goodbye. He could have left a note, or called, or SOMETHING. But instead he just walked out for two freaking years without a word. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><strong>Long story short, Sawyer was a huge huge huge jerk, and he never did anything to make me like him.</strong> He never did nice things for Reena, he never had sweet moments. He was always high out of his mind or drunk or having sex with her. This is going to sound so "disapproving parent" of me, but he was a bad influence. He was encouraging her to do drugs and skip class. And I know some teenagers are like that, but the key thing here is that Reena didn't want to do those things, and yet he kept pressuring her to. <strong>There was never a reason for Reena to like him.. she just did.</strong> It was pure lust, as far as I'm concerned. And on top of that, she had a great guy in the "after" chapters, but she ditched him to go running back to Sawyer. Why???<br /><br />As Sawyer became more and more of a dick, he knocked stars off my rating. As Reena kept running back to him, I lost sympathy for her. At first I felt bad for her because Sawyer ran out on her... but now... honestly.... she kind of had it coming. She stayed with this guy when he was nothing but disrespectful to her. He was always a flaky boyfriend, so it's no surprising that he just up and left one day.<br /><br /><strong>I feel like <em>How to Love</em> has all the makings of a really good book.</strong> It's well written, I like the alternating "before" and "after" chapters, and it's an interesting story. But it is completely ruined by Sawyer. He was a horrible character and slowly made me detest the book. And since Reena kept running back to him, I started to detest her as well. She also had this really annoying habit of raging at Sawyer for being a dick, and then when he'd say "What's wrong? Are you mad?" she'd lie and say nothing was wrong. So he'd be out flirting with other girls, she'd start acting bitchy towards him, he'd ask what the problem was, and she'd say NOTHING. <strong>She just let everything go and never stood up for herself.</strong><br /><br />If, somehow, you don't detest Sawyer, then I think it's really easy to love this book. But if you get as annoyed with his horrible doucheyness as I did, then it's kind of a book-ruiner. <strong>The problem is that <em>How to Love</em> is ALL about the romance and loving and all that, but when you have a horrible love interest, that just makes the book painful to read.</strong></span>
  <a data-text-id="2061690260237416182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1011939689" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1011939689" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1011939689?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=unhauled">unhauled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1011939689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7724350214017690317">3.5 stars<br/><br/>It's so hard for me to collect my thoughts about this book. I nearly unhauled this and at this point, I'm unable to determine if whether I should have or not. I kept this because I've never read a book on teen pregnancy before, and I really wanted to try this. I fell in love with the writing of this book. Katie Cotugno isn't necessarily the most brilliant writer, but she makes such clever analogies and her sentences flow so well that I was really rather impressed. And usually I hate now</span>
  <span id="freeText7724350214017690317" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />It's so hard for me to collect my thoughts about this book. I nearly unhauled this and at this point, I'm unable to determine if whether I should have or not. I kept this because I've never read a book on teen pregnancy before, and I really wanted to try this. I fell in love with the writing of this book. Katie Cotugno isn't necessarily the most brilliant writer, but she makes such clever analogies and her sentences flow so well that I was really rather impressed. And usually I hate now-and-then perspectives, but I actually felt like the Before and After layout of this book was done really well and I was never bored with one chapter or the other. These two factors by themselves, combined with the fact that I was genuinely enjoying the storyline at first, would have made it a five star book for me. But very quickly, I found myself really disliking Sawyer. And he, along with the negativity he brought into this book, is really what brought it down for me. He was a complete jerk and still expected to be loved, which I didn't agree with. There was so much angst--too much angst-- in the relationship between Sawyer and Reena that I was so exasperated and wished she would just dump him for good. Reena has a boyfriend in the "After" chapters, and I hated how Sawyer came onto her even though he knew that she was in a relationship. How he cruelly demanded that Reena tell him she loved him. I just never understood him or his motives or his personality, and since the book literally centers around their relationship, I found myself growing detached. <br /><br />Overall, this book was just an experience. I think it's really important because it handles the topic of teen pregnancy well. So well, that I was extremely uncomfortable reading this book at times. Not because it was graphic, but just because I was able to put myself in Reena's shoes for a moment and imagining myself in her situation was horrible. This book made me feel so vulnerable and gross, and I'm kind of impressed that it brought out that reaction in me. Putting this down, I seriously feel more concerned about making meaningful relationships and being responsible within those relationships. I can only imagine other teens reading this and feeling the same way; hopefully it touched someone to be able to see and understand how rough being a young mom is. It certainly enlightened me about the topic, and I'm left feeling grateful that I'm in a family of people who support me and that i'm single af and don't have to worry about Reena's situation happening to me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7724350214017690317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_717531476" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/717531476" />
    <a title="Gillian Berry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13535966-gillian-berry"><img alt="Gillian Berry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354328337p2/13535966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/717531476?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gillian Berry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gillian Berry" href="/user/show/13535966-gillian-berry">Gillian Berry</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=arcs-i-own">arcs-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=rep">rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=great-shelf-of-meh">great-shelf-of-meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=love-triangles-are-pointy">love-triangles-are-pointy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=should-have-liked-this-more">should-have-liked-this-more</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer717531476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12875631656493462260"><b>Rating:</b> I am SO VERY CONFLICTED ABOUT THIS BOOK. Honestly, getting my thoughts in any kind of order seems to be impossible. It's almost like I hated and loved this book in equal measure. In the end, I feel like the strengths of this book are so strong that they outweighed the negatives. The first half of this book is sensational. The second half made me mildly crabby.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380683969ra/3116400.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In an effort to make my thoughts more orderly, I'm going to impose some order on this review.<br/><br/><b>I loved:</b> The writing. <i>How to Love</i> is </span>
  <span id="freeText12875631656493462260" style="display:none"><b>Rating:</b> I am SO VERY CONFLICTED ABOUT THIS BOOK. Honestly, getting my thoughts in any kind of order seems to be impossible. It's almost like I hated and loved this book in equal measure. In the end, I feel like the strengths of this book are so strong that they outweighed the negatives. The first half of this book is sensational. The second half made me mildly crabby.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380683969ra/3116400.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In an effort to make my thoughts more orderly, I'm going to impose some order on this review.<br><br><b>I loved:</b> The writing. <i>How to Love</i> is written in first person from Reena's POV, and Reena is sharp and funny and observant. It was really easy to slip into the story and feel everything she was feeling. She's got a really great voice. And the narrative technique used was really interesting. There were two story threads--the Before, when Reena is in high school and Sawyer LeGrande is there, and the After, two years later when Sawyer LeGrande returns. I was surprised by how completely invested I was in the story, reading it nearly straight thought. Before tells the story of Reena and Sawyer falling in love and coming together, while the After starts with Reena, who has accepted her new life, dealing with the fact that the prodigal Sawyer is back in her life. The Before and After style created tiny mysteries that linked up really nicely, with the present echoing the past in nicely heartbreaking ways.<br><br><b>I hated:</b> Sawyer. Perhaps <i>hate</i> is a strong word. He's got a couple of swoony moments (loved Sawyer and Rina's talk on the swingset--I totally got the Sawyer Swoon there) , and I kind of understood him as a character. His parents expect a certain life out of him, a life he doesn't want to lead. He's not a bad guy, really, but he's utterly dysfunctional, and I thought it was pretty criminal the way he dragged Reena into his dysfunctionality. Sawyer is a couple of years older than Reena, and is the child of Reena's parents closest friends. They've grown up together, and Reena's been in love with him since nearly the beginning. (<i>Why</i>, beyond the fact that he's extraordinarily handsome, I'm not completely sure.) Then Saywer starts dating Reena's best friend, and for me, the Sawyer-appeal began to dissipate somewhat.<br><br><b>I loved:</b> Reena. I totally got this girl. She is the Good Catholic Daughter, the high achiever, the one nobody thought in a million years would get pregnant. She plays it pretty close to the vest, which is something I can relate to, doing everything she can not to make her true feelings about things known. Her family has been magnificently unfair to her, but she loves her daughter, Hannah, with all her heart. Before Hannah, she wanted to be a travel writer and go to Northwestern and see the bigger world outside her small Florida town. This book immerses us really well in Reena's mind, showing us her true desires and feelings. And because of all that, I would have loved this book if it hadn't been for the next point.<br><br><b>I hated:</b> Sawyer + Reena. It seemed like every single time Sayer and Reena interacted, he did something to hurt her. My particular favorite Sawyer moment was the first time they slept together (not a spoiler, they have a child), which happened to be the first time Reena had ever slept with <i>anybody</i>, and then Sawyer didn't call her. Or see her. For, like, three months. <i>And then never apologized</i>. He had other issues goes on, I got that, but I never thought Sawyer reached the right level of contrition for all the enormous harm he'd done to Reena (not just the pregancy thing. Admittedly, he didn't know Reena was pregnant when he took off, <i>but he still took off</i>). There's the time Sawyer pressures her to skip school. To betray her best friend. Let's not even mention what he does the night Reena gets into college.<br><br>I mean, I was basically rooting for girlfriend to<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380683969ra/3116401.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All of the really bad stuff is Before Sawyer. And Before Sawyer is not a healthy Sawyer. After Sawyer is way swoonier and way more put together, and I could have worked with this. I MUCH PREFERRED After Sawyer. I <i>almost</i> really, really liked him. But again... he didn't seem sorry enough! He just kind of waltzed back into town and was all offended that Reena was so mad at him. And I just wanted to scream "YOU ARE LUCKY YOU STILL HAVE ALL YOUR TOES, BUDDY, BE GRATEFUL FOR THAT."<br><br>Blegh. I'm sorry, guys. I just didn't feel this romance. Shelby, Reena's awesomesauce best friend, said it best that self-sufficient Reena forgets how "bad-ass" she is whenever Sayer, who done her wrong, turns his big emerald eyes on her. BLEGH.<br><br><b>I loved:</b> Everything else. The narrative technique, the way Cotugno portrayed family dynamics, and the particular family dynamics of a high-achieving Catholic teenager getting pregnant at sixteen. Extra points for a loving stepmother, minus points for a mostly invisible brother, a bajillion points for Shelby the awesome-- if judgmental--lesbian best friend who tries to tell Reena to GET A GRIP. I loved the scene where Reena finally lets out all the feelings she's been keeping inside since she got pregnant, basically letting her father and Sawyer's parents have it (<i>now if only she'd done this to Sawyer too</i>).<br><br>Most people are really going to love this book. It has a lot going for it, and I will definitely read whatever Cotugno writes next. I truly loved her writing. But when you read a love story and can't truly invest<b> </b>in, well, the love story part, there's no way you can give that book all the stars. I'm pretty bummed about it. With a few tweaks, this could have been one of my favorite reads of the year. I was totally engrossed in it, and the characters were vivid, and it was equal parts funny and heartbreaking (even a tad melodramatic). I recommend giving it a shot, if only so we can have conversations about stomping on Sawyer LeGrande's feet.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12875631656493462260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2132275894" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2132275894" />
    <a title="Joce (squibblesreads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48087215-joce-squibblesreads"><img alt="Joce (squibblesreads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445310967p2/48087215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2132275894?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joce (squibblesreads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joce (squibblesreads)" href="/user/show/48087215-joce-squibblesreads">Joce (squibblesreads)</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2132275894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5375127413487953230">Teens making out against a wall. Character makes joke about terrorists. Then asks another character "are you one of those people who are really sensitive about terrorist jokes?" <br/>The scene was pretty much left at that. I tried to continue but I'll cool it w books w privileged characters that make offhand remarks about terrorism with not a smidgen of recourse either directly or indirectly. Hard pass.<br/>Edit: I read a tiny bit more and it doesn't seem as though this character is made out to be villain</span>
  <span id="freeText5375127413487953230" style="display:none">Teens making out against a wall. Character makes joke about terrorists. Then asks another character "are you one of those people who are really sensitive about terrorist jokes?" <br />The scene was pretty much left at that. I tried to continue but I'll cool it w books w privileged characters that make offhand remarks about terrorism with not a smidgen of recourse either directly or indirectly. Hard pass.<br />Edit: I read a tiny bit more and it doesn't seem as though this character is made out to be villainous, ignorant, or unaware. The person she was talking to was our protagonist who I believe is written to be sympathetic, and the remark was a device to amplify the protagonist's "sensitivity" to seeing the characters making out, which I believe makes it even more harmful.<br /><br />Edit again: Finished this so people wouldn’t come at me for not finishing it when I include it in a list in an upcoming video. Wasn’t worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5375127413487953230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1149028215" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1149028215" />
    <a title="Maria " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5769334-maria"><img alt="Maria " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600318539p2/5769334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1149028215?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria " href="/user/show/5769334-maria">Maria </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782060000" href="/book/show/18113193-how-to-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5769334-maria?shelf=books-i-love-to-death">books-i-love-to-death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5769334-maria?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5769334-maria?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5769334-maria?shelf=slice-of-life">slice-of-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5769334-maria?shelf=shove-it-in-your-face-recs">shove-it-in-your-face-recs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5769334-maria?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5769334-maria?shelf=fave-heroine">fave-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5769334-maria?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5769334-maria?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5769334-maria?shelf=douchebag-hero">douchebag-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1149028215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17196100601597028448"><br/><br/><b>
  <u>REACTION AFTER READING THE BOOK</u>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420841089ra/13276911.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420841229ra/13276926.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>The end made me so damn happy for Reena and Sawyer.</b><br/><br/>This book was not perfect. It has some shortcomings, but personally I thought this book was great. I think it dealt with the topic of teenage pregnancy realistically. <b>I should know because I have been in that situation.</b> I have been Reena at some point in my life, and I could definitely say that most of the situations Reena went through in this book was accurate. <br/><br/>I've read a couple of negative reviews about this</span>
  <span id="freeText17196100601597028448" style="display:none"><br><br><b>
  <u>REACTION AFTER READING THE BOOK</u>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420841089ra/13276911.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420841229ra/13276926.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The end made me so damn happy for Reena and Sawyer.</b><br><br>This book was not perfect. It has some shortcomings, but personally I thought this book was great. I think it dealt with the topic of teenage pregnancy realistically. <b>I should know because I have been in that situation.</b> I have been Reena at some point in my life, and I could definitely say that most of the situations Reena went through in this book was accurate. <br><br>I've read a couple of negative reviews about this book and they were complaining about Sawyer being a douchebag. And I agree, he is a douchebag. But that's the entire point of the <b>Before and After</b> POVs from Reena. You get to see the <b>"what happened"</b> and the <b>"why he left"</b> and also the <b>"how different is he now".</b><br><br>But I'm not going to elaborate on that now. Let's start with the gist first.<br><br><b>
  <u>HOW IT STARTS</u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I've been looking for Sawyer for half a lifetime when I find him standing in front of the Slurpee machine at the 7-Eleven on Federal Highway, gazing through the window at the frozen, neon-bright churning like he's expecting the mysteries of the universe to be revealed to him from inside.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>
  <u>THE GIST</u>
</b><br><br>Reena and Sawyer practically grew up together. Their families are basically one family, because of a joint business their parents have. Reena always liked Sawyer, but she has always been too scared to act on those feelings. So she just let it go.<br><br>Reena had a bright future ahead of her. She was smart and very studious. She was taking advanced classes and is actually about to graduate earlier than she should be. But what she wasn't expecting was being with Sawyer. And being with Sawyer was not what she expected. It was good, for the most part, but there were other things that she did not know about Sawyer that she had to accept, because she likes him.<br><br>So... the thing happened. You guys know what I mean. Right? <br><br>Yeah so it happened and well she got pregnant at 16.<br><br>And Sawyer.<br><br>He left. Without saying a word.<br><br><b>
  <u>MEET THE CHARACTERS</u>
</b><br><br><b>Reena</b><br><br><i>Serena or Reena is a great character. She made some mistakes, but that's all part of life isn't it? And that's what made this book great. </i> <b>The characters were flawed and imperfect. You don't go into a teenage pregnancy book and think that the main character is a Mary Sue.</b> No that does not happen. These kids obviously did something stupid and immature, hence why this is a teenage pregnancy book and not just your typical romance book.<br><br>I read a few reviews saying that she was well immature and all that stuff. She's not. <b>She's actually more mature and independent than I was when I got pregnant.</b> I got pregnant when I was eighteen and a mom at 19. I was an adult. But to be honest, she handled things pretty well on her own than I did. I was a mess. I was crap. I was useless. And that's the reality of being a teenage mom. There were times that she made crappy decisions like with Aaron, but give her a break. <b>People makes mistakes, not just people who got pregnant early whose baby daddy comes back and now they don't know what to do. That also happens to people who doesn't have kids.</b> Let's not be too judgemental.<br><br>Although, there are a lot of things that happened to Reena that didn't happen to me, I still connected to her in a deeper level than I was ready for. I cried, especially on the confrontation scene with her Dad. <b>That was just... me. It was like that was me. And it did happen to me too so... I guess that's why that made me cry.</b><br><br><b>Sawyer</b><br><br>Now this dude is a dick. I agree. He had some stupid decisions. He's done stuff he shouldn't have. He treated Reena like crap on some occasions. <b>But he is not a bad person. </b> On the before POVs that is. If you've read the after POVs closely, you'll get why he left. I actually like the transitions of the Before and After POVs because it explains what is happening in the present. And it totally made sense for him to leave. <br><br>Do you guys want to know what type of guy is real douchebag? <b>THE ONE WHO LEAVES, DOESN'T SAY GOODBYE AND DOESN'T RETURN OR THE ONE WHO KNOWS YOU GOT PREGNANT BUT LEAVES ANYWAYS WITHOUT EVEN A CARE.</b> And Sawyer wasn't either of those. He left, that's true, but he had a very valid reason. I should know. <br><br><b>I like Sawyer. I really do. He's just one of those kids who is so pressured into doing everything right, that he is intentionally doing things wrong.</b> I could relate to that too. Although, I don't do drugs and all that crappy crap, but the pressure of doing what your expected to do is pretty heavy especially when you as a person would like to do something else. And that is what Sawyer's burden was.<br><br>Also, people change. And I liked seeing that with Sawyer's character. You'll see the contrast of who he was then and who he was currently. I thought his character was pretty well played.<br><br><b>The Parents</b><br><br>I felt that Katie also made it a point to include the conflic these two had with their parents and I really liked that. I would have to say that both of their parents were crap, but happy that Reena's father at least was able to redeem themselves.<br><br><b>
  <u>THE ROMANCE</u>
</b><br><br>It was very well played for me. <b>I felt that it was not perfect but it was good</b>. Reena and Sawyer obviously really liked each other. There were just some situations that stood in the way which prevented them from being together earlier and letting Allie (Reena's no good friend) having Sawyer first.<br><br>But I don't want to talk about that. I want to emphasize on the fact that they were responsible people that has feelings. If Sawyer knew, I think he wouldn't have left.<b> I honestly don't understand how people could think that just because someone hurts you, you can shut down all your feelings for that person.</b> You can't!!! Especially not when you share something as important as a kid. You can hate him/her at some point, but at the end of the day, you shared something special with that person and you can't hate them forever. And Reena did not forget that. She made it so clear to Sawyer that she was not okay with him being back a couple of times.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"You can't just come here after all this time and try to joke around with me and act like nother happened. That's not - Stuff happene, Sawyer. You can't just be back.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>And it was hard for Reena. You'll see her struggle about her conflicted feelings. <b>Aaron was easy and Sawyer was complicated.</b> She could just stay with Aaron, but will that make her completely happy? Will it be okay for her to stay on the safe side and not risk the chance of her having a complete family and be happy? Will you? <br><br>And Sawyer, I think I'm going to spoil you guys a bit, didn't know Reena was pregnant okay? He didn't fucking know. My douchebag of an ex-bf did know. And you know what? He left anyways. That's my basis of douchebaggery. <b>So forgive me if I don't think Sawyer is a big douchebag. He is far from it.</b> He's just a person who made lots of crazy mistakes that he is currently trying to ammend.<br><br>So do I think Sawyer and Reena should be together? Yes. Why? Well because they didn't split up because they wanted to anyways. They still had feelings for each other so there's really no reason why they couldn't work that out to have a complete family with their baby Hannah.<br><br><b>
  <u>FINAL THOUGHTS<u></u></u>
</b><br><br>I loved this book so much and happy that I read it first. It is not for everyone I get it, but luckily it was for me. I get all those things that happened to Reena and I think that's why I loved it more than I should have. <br><br>This book was about love, mistakes, and making up for those mistakes. It's about forgiveness. Trust. Family. There were a lot of good points on this book that really touched me. The characters all had their own struggles and demons to face. <br><br><b>How to love</b> is not only about loving a significant other. It's about loving your parents, your daughter, your friend. And I totally loved that. So much love. It reminded me of <b>If I Stay by Gale Forman</b> in some ways because of the different types of love that was shown in this book. I thought the plot twists were just placed at the right times.<br><br>This book made me real emotional. Emotional in a way that was good. I liked reading about people owning up to their mistakes and correcting their paths. Reena may have not been in the college of her choice, but at least she is still making something out of her life. And that goes with Sawyer too. That's why he came back. <br><br><b>Fresh start. And I think everyone deserves that.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17196100601597028448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_613490324" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/613490324" />
    <a title="Jaime Arkin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293701-jaime-arkin"><img alt="Jaime Arkin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303353688p2/5293701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/613490324?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaime Arkin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaime Arkin" href="/user/show/5293701-jaime-arkin">Jaime Arkin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=on-my-real-shelves">on-my-real-shelves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=ebook-format">ebook-format</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=true-5-starers">true-5-starers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=stand-alone-books">stand-alone-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=friends-to-more">friends-to-more</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=recommend-forever">recommend-forever</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer613490324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3422628478243991485">I seriously have started and stopped writing this review about 4 times. I'm sucking it up now and completing it though. <br/><br/>Every once in a while I read a book that totally exceeds anything I was expecting… a book that leaves you practically speechless with how incredibly it is written and the story it tells. That is what How To Love was for me. I’m not entirely sure what I can say about this book right now, so forgive me if none of this makes a bit of sense. <br/> <br/>First of all, it’s told in a wonderfull</span>
  <span id="freeText3422628478243991485" style="display:none">I seriously have started and stopped writing this review about 4 times. I'm sucking it up now and completing it though. <br><br>Every once in a while I read a book that totally exceeds anything I was expecting… a book that leaves you practically speechless with how incredibly it is written and the story it tells. That is what How To Love was for me. I’m not entirely sure what I can say about this book right now, so forgive me if none of this makes a bit of sense. <br> <br>First of all, it’s told in a wonderfully unique way. You get the before and after. Before and after what you ask? Well, before and after the whirlwind that is Sawyer LeGrande.<br> <br>Reena has loved Sawyer LeGrande for what seems like ever. She and her best friend Allie have watched and daydreamed about him forever. Sawyer, who is a few years older than them, has never seemed to notice. Until he does. Only it’s not Reena who captures his attention it seems. So when she loses her best friend over a stupid fight she focuses instead on her dreams. Graduating from high school a year early and getting early admittance to Northwestern are her big focus. She has dreams of traveling the world and becoming a travel writer and she knows she will succeed. <br> <br>Then something devastating happens… she loses the friend she never had the chance to make amends with. And then she finds herself pulled into Sawyer’s crazy life, and Sawyer isn’t exactly the perfect person she’s created in her mind. Six months later, he’s gone and she’s now trapped in a life she didn’t want or see for herself… her dreams of leaving and making something of herself down the drain.<br> <br>Almost three years later, Reena has accepted her new life, and while Sawyer disappeared without a word, she finds herself in a new relationship with that of her daughter Hannah. Only, things of course can’t be easy. She feels as though her father hates her. Raised in a very Catholic household, the news that she was pregnant was not one of celebration. But Reena has taken each hit and every disappointment in stride, hiding her anger and sadness in order to keep the peace. Sawyer’s parents who were once staples in her life have basically disappeared.<br> <br>Suddenly, Sawyer is back and she isn’t sure how to handle it. To say she has mixed feelings would be an understatement.<br> <br>AND That’s kind of all I want to tell you about the plot.<br> <br>So let’s talk about the things I fell in love with.<br> <br>Reena. This girl had me feeling every single damn thing. But I think what I loved most about her was that yes, this thing happens but instead of letting it ruin her, she is strong and she is determined and she is in love with this unexpected gift. I loved that even though she was so young, and believe me, she at times acted her age, but when she HAD to grow up... she did. And she did it with so much determination.<br> <br>Sawyer... man I really wanted to dislike him. I mean the way he's portrayed and the things he does. *I'm shaking my head right now* BUT I couldn't. Cotugno writes him in a way that while yes, at times I was angry with him, you also can't help but have a soft spot for him. As the chapters progress and his own story unfolds, I found my opinion of him changing. Things aren't always as they seem on the outside.<br><br><i>"Nothing about you, my dear, has ever been lost on me."</i> &lt;---I Love this quote from him. <br> <br>Shelby is the kind of best friend that every person needs in their lives and I absolutely love that we aren't subjected to the best friend who turns mean girl in this one. She stood by Serena through everything ... and I mean everything. And I loved her for it. Even Allie was written as a wonderful best friend and I love seeing this in YA. (Not every girl has an inner mean girl!) <br> <br>The story itself is just beautifully written in my opinion. Cotugno has created these incredibly flawed and realistic characters that you just can't help but fall for. I experienced all the emotions possible while reading this... tears, laughs, frustration, anger and yes even some swoons, and the writing style was perfect. <br><br>Sometimes I feel that people go into every single book expecting non-stop action and adventure which is fine... but this isn't that. This is one of those stories that has a gentle telling, a soft sort of true to life calm about it. It's compelling and beautiful and also a little bit heartbreaking... with an ending that had me smiling like an idiot. <br><br>I can't recommend this book enough, it's quickly moved up to all-time favorite status. <br><br>Thank you to Harpercollins and Edelweiss for the advance copy for review.<br><br>This review can be found on my blog, Fic Fare: <br><a href="http://fictionfare.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380223306ra/681029.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer664988565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17493556759978833232">I'm sorry if this comes out as a rant.. You have been warned..<br/><br/>Nothing really happens exactly..It's just day to day mundane things except at the end there was a bit of drama. There's no hook to keep you reading. I pushed this aside twice and picked it up again just so I can find out if he changes. There are chapters of her going to the mall and shopping and cooking food. It's super mundane and utterly boring. I also don't like the Before and After chapters because it breaks the momentum of whatev</span>
  <span id="freeText17493556759978833232" style="display:none">I'm sorry if this comes out as a rant.. You have been warned..<br /><br />Nothing really happens exactly..It's just day to day mundane things except at the end there was a bit of drama. There's no hook to keep you reading. I pushed this aside twice and picked it up again just so I can find out if he changes. There are chapters of her going to the mall and shopping and cooking food. It's super mundane and utterly boring. I also don't like the Before and After chapters because it breaks the momentum of whatever happened. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And these two start their relationship by cheating. With her best friend's BOYFRIEND. WHAT THE EFF?!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I dislike Sawyer soo much. Reena is supposed to be this smart girl but she keeps going back for more. She keeps putting up with his crap. Not only during the Before, but also with the After. Thought she learned her lesson? And the moment when we find out happens with Allie and Sawyer? Is this supposed to be the reason why he was acting out the entire time? I thought he was already a jerk before that. Then there's the sweet and steady Aaron who wants her. Yet she wants the bad-boy Sawyer. Every time he would smirk I wanted to punch him. Ughhh I did not like him at all. He's probably one of the worst YA boyfriends I've read about. Did I miss something??? Wasn't this supposed to be some epic love story? I found it to be more like lust!? I didn't find anything remotely interesting or passionate about these two. I'm sorely disappointed.. *sighs*<br /><br />I'm guessing there was supposed to be so much more than just romantic love, but also family and friendship love. But again I didn't find any of that. Her best friend Shelby keeps forgiving her for things and she didn't even reach out to her. Talk about no effort. And obviously coming from a strict Catholic family she would have trouble being sixteen and pregnant, but good God she did not handle it well. Blowing up at her father that way. That's pretty disrespectful to do to your parent. I wished there was more of an emphasis about how terrified she would be of having this baby at her age, and how her faith could help or destroy her. Yet there wasn't any of that. It was all Sawyer goggles from then on. <br /><br />I'm so sad I didn't like this..It's always hard to like a book when you dislike the characters.. Maybe someone else will have better luck than I did?<br /><br />RATING 2/5<br /><br />QUOTES<br /><br />Why did you only love me when I was good? (256)<br /><br />I could t figure out how he could make me so happy and so miserable all at once. (308)<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1672096934?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37103769-rachel-maniacup?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1672096934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17724414832917570010">This is my first book of <b>Katie Catugno</b>,and I must say that this author is a talented writer because she writes beautifully..I just didn't like the story line because it didn't much portrayed what the title says(and it's the title that captivated me into reading this). I'm not being judgmental but I guess,I have high hopes and expectations when it comes to contemporary. I thought,the story would flow similarly to "Before We Were Strangers" or something like the "First Comes Love"series-these are </span>
  <span id="freeText17724414832917570010" style="display:none">This is my first book of <b>Katie Catugno</b>,and I must say that this author is a talented writer because she writes beautifully..I just didn't like the story line because it didn't much portrayed what the title says(and it's the title that captivated me into reading this). I'm not being judgmental but I guess,I have high hopes and expectations when it comes to contemporary. I thought,the story would flow similarly to "Before We Were Strangers" or something like the "First Comes Love"series-these are stories that show us how to really love someone may that be a friend,family,a career,or a lover,and how they are all blended or connected for better or worse.<br /><br />And though I didn't like this much,I had to admit that I found this a refreshing read,because there were parts that I adored in the story. One of them is the way <b>Reena</b>, the female <b>MC</b>, handled being a single parent from pregnancy to raising her baby all by herself. She is one tough young lady who suffered a lot of emotions,because of her obsession/love to <b>Sawyer</b>,the father of her baby, <b>Hannah</b>. <br /><br />The author is absolutely a master of playing reader's emotions,'cause I did cry several times in this book.So,yeah..I'm definitely looking forward to more of Catugno's novels..<br />Many thanks to my dear little sister,who is always so kind of lending me her books.You may also check her wonderful review on this,which she enjoyed more than I did.^^</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_621555500" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621555500" />
    <a title="Katy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4572741-katy"><img alt="Katy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365039295p2/4572741.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621555500?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy" href="/user/show/4572741-katy">Katy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621555500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer448030120865203091">Okay, so this wasn't the light, cute, fun read I was looking for, but wow, this book was pretty good. What a great story that realistically portrays a situation that happens all-too-often in a way that captures your heart.<br/><br/>The reason I liked this story so much was because it wasn't about a girl in a rough or trashy neighborhood that got pregnant by the typical bad boy. Serena and Sawyer are from devout Christian families, and they deal with issues that real teens deal with - whether it's Serena's</span>
  <span id="freeText448030120865203091" style="display:none">Okay, so this wasn't the light, cute, fun read I was looking for, but wow, this book was pretty good. What a great story that realistically portrays a situation that happens all-too-often in a way that captures your heart.<br /><br />The reason I liked this story so much was because it wasn't about a girl in a rough or trashy neighborhood that got pregnant by the typical bad boy. Serena and Sawyer are from devout Christian families, and they deal with issues that real teens deal with - whether it's Serena's studious attempt to graduate a year early so she can leave town or Sawyer finding escape through music and other substances. Maybe Allie's and Leo's situations were a bit too much, but I think they were both necessary, especially the latter, to kind of make the story work.<br /><br />And I really connected with Serena in this book. Yeah, she was a bit stand-offish at the beginning, but if I were a private person who had a friend like Allie, I would probably be that way too. Don't get me wrong, Serena did come across as a bitch for a good portion of this book. But at the same time, she really does go through a lot, and I can't imagine having to deal with the situations that she's had to face - with Sawyer, with the baby, with her family's change, with moving on. And she made her fair share of stupid actions, but you can't help who you fall in love with sometimes, and really, I can't see it ending up any other way for her.<br /><br />The romance itself was realistically good. Serena and Sawyer both had their great moments, making them wonderful companions. At the same time, they had their fair share of arguments - over stupid things, over ridiculous things, over legitimate things, real issues that couples deal with all the time.<br /><br />I wish I got to know Lydia more and why she decide not to be there for Serena, and what Roger's problem was with Sawyer. And Cade was there, but not. I really love Soledad and Shelby (although I did feel that fact about her at the end just came from nowhere), and it was heartwarming to see Serena patch things up with Leo. And Aaron - it breaks my heart.<br /><br />Overall, it was refreshing to read something that happens enough but does not get enough attention - but in such a way where you can actually connect with the characters. Props to Cotugno on her debut.<br /><br />Previously: I am on a YA chick-lit binge/marathon - in desperate need of a GOOD cute, fluffy read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="448030120865203091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1380382843" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1380382843" />
    <a title="Sky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32831460-sky"><img alt="Sky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590554430p2/32831460.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1380382843?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sky" href="/user/show/32831460-sky">Sky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>
